<p><b>Aaron James Ramsey</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born 26 December 1990)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-date_of_birth_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-date_of_birth-1">[1]</a></sup> is a Welsh professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales national team</a>. Ramsey mainly plays as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Box-to-box_midfielder" title="Midfielder">box-to-box midfielder</a>, but has also been deployed on the left and right <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">wings</a>. He played as a schoolboy for <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>, where he spent eight years in youth football, became the club's youngest ever first team player, and made 22 appearances for the senior team – including the <a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">2008 FA Cup Final</a>.</p>
<p>Ramsey moved to Arsenal in 2008 in a £5 million deal, where he quickly gained first team experience. However, his career stalled significantly after he suffered a broken leg in a match against <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> in February 2010. After two loan spells away from Arsenal, he returned to full fitness and re-established himself as a regular starter during the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Arsenal_F.C._season" title="2011–12 Arsenal F.C. season">2011–12 season</a>. Ramsey was a key player for Arsenal in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Arsenal_F.C._season" title="2013–14 Arsenal F.C. season">2013–14 season</a> campaign, scoring 16 goals in all competitions, including the winner in the <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Cup_Final" title="2014 FA Cup Final">2014 FA Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>.</p>
<p>Ramsey made his full international debut for Wales in 2008, and was part of their successful <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a> qualification campaign, where he was included in the Team of the Tournament. He also represented <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Olympic_football_team" title="Great Britain Olympic football team">Great Britain</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament">2012 Olympics</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Style_of_play"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Style of play</span></a></li>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As a child, Ramsey attended <a href="/wiki/Ysgol_Gyfun_Cwm_Rhymni" title="Ysgol Gyfun Cwm Rhymni">Ysgol Gyfun Cwm Rhymni</a> (Rhymney Valley Comprehensive School) in <a href="/wiki/Caerphilly_County_Borough" title="Caerphilly County Borough">Caerphilly County Borough</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Ramsey's first introduction to football was at the age of nine, when he attended a <a href="/wiki/Urdd_Gobaith_Cymru" title="Urdd Gobaith Cymru">Urdd</a> training session at <a href="/wiki/Caerphilly" title="Caerphilly">Caerphilly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Before turning to football, he was a keen rugby player and athlete. As a schoolboy he played as a winger for Caerphilly R.F.C.s youth development programme, where he was approached by scouts from <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> side <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Helens_RFC" title="St Helens RFC">St Helens</a> after playing in a youth match against them<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> but had already been signed by Cardiff City's youth academy. Ramsey was Welsh Schools' Athletic Association <a href="/wiki/Pentathlon" title="Pentathlon">pentathlon</a> champion in 2005 and was ranked 4th in <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> in the under 17 age group in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> He lived with his parents, Marlene and Kevin, and his brother, Josh, until moving to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> where he was housemates with former Cardiff City teammate, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Gunter" title="Chris Gunter">Chris Gunter</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> who was then playing for <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>. Ramsey is <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">bilingual</a>, speaking both <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardiff_City">Cardiff City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cardiff City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey.png"><img alt="Alt text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1033" data-file-width="442" height="351" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Aaron_Ramsey.png/150px-Aaron_Ramsey.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Aaron_Ramsey.png/225px-Aaron_Ramsey.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Aaron_Ramsey.png/300px-Aaron_Ramsey.png 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ramsey at <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After impressing in an <a href="/wiki/Urdd_Gobaith_Cymru" title="Urdd Gobaith Cymru">Urdd</a> tournament as a youngster he signed for <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>, who beat off competition from <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, as a schoolboy at the age of eight, working his way through the club's youth system. After a few more years he eventually made his Cardiff City début in the last home game of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Football_League_2006-07" title="The Football League 2006-07">2006–07 Championship season</a>, coming on to replace <a href="/wiki/Paul_Parry" title="Paul Parry">Paul Parry</a> in the final minute of the 1–0 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a> on 28 April 2007. In doing so, Ramsey became the youngest player to ever play for Cardiff City, aged just 16 years and 124 days,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> beating the previous record holder <a href="/wiki/John_Toshack" title="John Toshack">John Toshack</a>. In June 2007, Cardiff City turned down a bid of over £1m for Ramsey from a London-based Premier League club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The club was not named, but it was widely believed that they continued to watch Ramsey at every available opportunity during the 2007–08 season. Cardiff also turned down a £1m offer, although the deal was to start with a payment of £200,000 and rise depending on his future achievements, from <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>.</p>
<p>Ramsey made his first league appearance of the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Cardiff_City_F.C._season" title="2007–08 Cardiff City F.C. season">2007–08 season</a> on 6 October, when he came on as a late substitute for <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink" title="Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink">Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink</a> in the 2–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>. Ramsey signed his first professional contract in December 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and went on to make his first full professional start for Cardiff on 5 January in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> against <a href="/wiki/Chasetown_F.C." title="Chasetown F.C.">Chasetown</a> replacing the suspended <a href="/wiki/Stephen_McPhail" title="Stephen McPhail">Stephen McPhail</a>. An impressive performance from Ramsey saw him head in the second Cardiff goal as they went on to win 3–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Due to his performance against Chasetown, Ramsey was nominated for the Player of the Round award, eventually losing out to <a href="/wiki/Coventry_City_F.C." title="Coventry City F.C.">Coventry's</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Mifsud" title="Michael Mifsud">Michael Mifsud</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> On 26 April, he scored his first league goal in a 3–3 draw against Burnley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> He went on to make his first career league start three weeks later in a 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> and began to establish himself in the first team, making several more starts in the Cardiff side. He made a total of 22 appearances during the season, his first full season of professional football, and played in five of the club's six <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_FA_Cup" title="2007–08 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> matches, including <a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">the final</a>, becoming the second youngest player to play in an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a> after <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Weston" title="Curtis Weston">Curtis Weston</a>, who played in the <a href="/wiki/2004_FA_Cup_Final" title="2004 FA Cup Final">2004 FA Cup Final</a> for <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following Ramsey's impressive performance in the 2–1 FA Cup quarter-final win over <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> it was revealed that <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Sir Alex Ferguson</a> had talked to Cardiff boss <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dave_Jones_(football_manager)" title="Dave Jones (football manager)">Dave Jones</a> to inquire about Ramsey, who were later joined by <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> in following his progress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Ramsey in fact grew up a Manchester United fan, but in the end he decided not to join them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Cardiff Chairman <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ridsdale" title="Peter Ridsdale">Peter Ridsdale</a> told the BBC that Arsenal's bid of £5 million up front had been accepted. Arsenal's bid did not include a loan clause that would allow Ramsey to stay at Cardiff for another season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Cardiff City assistant manager and former Arsenal player and coach <a href="/wiki/Terry_Burton" title="Terry Burton">Terry Burton</a>, who was credited for having brought through Ramsey, also helped recommend him to Arsenal manager <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a>, having retained a longstanding connection to the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-19">[19]</a></sup> During the transfer negotiations, Burton also advised that Ramsey join Arsenal, citing the similarity between the player and the club's overall style of play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arsenal">Arsenal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Arsenal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 10 June 2008 it was confirmed that after meeting officials from Arsenal, Everton and Manchester United, Ramsey had decided to join Arsenal, who paid Cardiff City a total of £4.8 million for the player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arsenal_claim_discount_on_Ramsey_deal_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arsenal_claim_discount_on_Ramsey_deal-20">[20]</a></sup> The move was completed on 13 June 2008 on what is said to be a long-term contract. The main reason he chose Arsenal ahead of the other clubs that pursued his signature was the approach of Arsenal manager <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a>, who flew him and his family to <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> to talk about the plans Wenger had for him and his potential future with Arsenal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramsey_completes_Arsenal_switch_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ramsey_completes_Arsenal_switch-21">[21]</a></sup> Wenger described Ramsey as "a player with a fantastic engine, good build, good technique and good vision".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arsenal_end_of_2008-09_season_walkabout.jpg"><img alt="Alt text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Arsenal_end_of_2008-09_season_walkabout.jpg/300px-Arsenal_end_of_2008-09_season_walkabout.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Arsenal_end_of_2008-09_season_walkabout.jpg/450px-Arsenal_end_of_2008-09_season_walkabout.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Arsenal_end_of_2008-09_season_walkabout.jpg/600px-Arsenal_end_of_2008-09_season_walkabout.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arsenal_end_of_2008-09_season_walkabout.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ramsey (in dark blue) at the end of the 2008–09 campaign</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ramsey made his competitive début for Arsenal in the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2008–09 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> third qualifying round against <a href="/wiki/FC_Twente" title="FC Twente">FC Twente</a> on 13 August 2008 and his league début a month later against <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> on 13 September 2008, marking it with an assist to <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Adebayor" title="Emmanuel Adebayor">Emmanuel Adebayor</a> for Arsenal's fourth and Adebayor's third. On 23 September 2008 he completed 90 minutes in Arsenal's third round <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> game against <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> where he added two more assists to his season's tally, setting up <a href="/wiki/Nicklas_Bendtner" title="Nicklas Bendtner">Nicklas Bendtner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Vela" title="Carlos Vela">Carlos Vela</a>, which Arsenal won 6–0. He scored his first goal for the club in their 5–2 victory away against <a href="/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e_S.K." title="Fenerbahçe S.K.">Fenerbahçe</a> in the group stages of the UEFA Champions League<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> by shooting a long range shot which hit the post and went in, becoming the fifth youngest scorer in Champions League history, and only the second player born in the 1990s to score a Champions League goal. Ramsey was named amongst a host of young players poised to shine in 2009 by Fifa.com.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> On 1 July 2009, he signed a new long-term contract at Arsenal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 August 2009, Ramsey scored his first league goal in a one-on-one against goalkeeper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_James_(footballer)" title="David James (footballer)">David James</a> as Arsenal beat <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> 4–1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Stadium" title="Emirates Stadium">Emirates Stadium</a> and then set up <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Arshavin" title="Andrey Arshavin">Andrey Arshavin</a> in a 3–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League_2009%E2%80%9310_play-off_round" title="UEFA Champions League 2009–10 play-off round">Champions League play-offs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In the 28 October <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Football_League_Cup" title="2008–09 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> fourth round win against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, he produced an impressive performance and set up <a href="/wiki/Nicklas_Bendtner" title="Nicklas Bendtner">Nicklas Bendtner</a> that earned him the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Man_of_the_Match" title="Man of the Match">Man of the Match</a> award.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey_Stoke_City_FC_V_Arsenal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="388" data-file-width="243" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Aaron_Ramsey_Stoke_City_FC_V_Arsenal.jpg/200px-Aaron_Ramsey_Stoke_City_FC_V_Arsenal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/89/Aaron_Ramsey_Stoke_City_FC_V_Arsenal.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey_Stoke_City_FC_V_Arsenal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ramsey playing against <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ramsey made his first <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> start of the season on 7 November 2009 as Arsenal beat <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> 4–1 at <a href="/wiki/Molineux_Stadium" title="Molineux Stadium">Molineux</a> with Ramsey completing 90-minutes for the first time in the top-flight. Four days after the game, he was awarded the Welsh Young Player of the Year award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> On 5 December 2009, Ramsey scored his second league goal of the season in a comfortable 2–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a>. On 30 December, Ramsey went on to score his third goal of the season, along with an assist in the 4–1 victory against <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>. On 3 January 2010, Ramsey scored a 78th-minute equaliser in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_FA_Cup" title="2009–10 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> third round tie against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Boleyn_Ground" title="Boleyn Ground">Upton Park</a>. Arsenal went on to win the tie 2–1, with <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_da_Silva" title="Eduardo da Silva">Eduardo</a> scoring an 83rd-minute header. Ramsey went on to be named <a href="/wiki/E.ON" title="E.ON">E.ON</a> Man of the Match. Ramsey has been described by manager <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> as: "An offence-minded <a href="/wiki/Roy_Keane" title="Roy Keane">Roy Keane</a>" and "an all-round player, with a fantastic ability to cover distances."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 February 2010, Arsenal played Stoke City at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Britannia_Stadium" title="Britannia Stadium">Britannia Stadium</a>, where a tackle by Stoke defender <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Shawcross" title="Ryan Shawcross">Ryan Shawcross</a> caused a double fracture in Ramsey's lower right leg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Ramsey was hospitalised, and it was later confirmed that he had broken his <a href="/wiki/Tibia" title="Tibia">tibia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fibula" title="Fibula">fibula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> No return date was initially given,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> but it was announced on 20 March that he started walking without his crutches. Ramsey signed a new long-term contract with Arsenal on 1 June 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> He returned to training in October 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> On 23 November 2010, Ramsey made his return to football for the Arsenal reserve team against the Wolverhampton Wanderers reserve team at Arsenal's London Colney training ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Loan_to_Nottingham_Forest">Loan to Nottingham Forest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Loan to Nottingham Forest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ramsey was loaned out to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest" title="Nottingham Forest">Nottingham Forest</a> on 25 November 2010 until 3 January 2011. The move was to allow him to gain match fitness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Ramsey made his Forest debut on 29 November 2010 as a 61st-minute substitute against Leicester City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> He made his first start against <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C.%E2%80%93Nottingham_Forest_F.C._rivalry" title="Derby County F.C.–Nottingham Forest F.C. rivalry">East Midlands derby</a> where he played 60 minutes. The match ended 5–2 to Nottingham Forest. Due to adverse weather conditions, Ramsey was limited to just five appearances for Forest before returning to Arsenal in January 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Ramsey returned to Arsenal on 5 January 2011 before the club's <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_FA_Cup" title="2010–11 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> tie against <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> in which he was an unused substitute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Ramsey was also an unused substitute at Portman Road on 12 January for the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Football_League_Cup" title="2010–11 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> semi-final against <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Town_F.C." title="Ipswich Town F.C.">Ipswich Town</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardiff_.28loan.29">Cardiff (loan)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Cardiff (loan)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:33%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">
<p>The difference in his strength and his maturity – both on and off the pitch – was amazing. It really was a case of someone leaving as a boy and coming back as a man ... He is so strong mentally, and he certainly hasn't been holding anything back.</p>
</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">— Cardiff boss Dave Jones on Ramsey's loan return to the club<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Ramsey returned to Cardiff City in a one-month loan move in order to gain match fitness,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> joining former Arsenal youngster <a href="/wiki/Jay_Emmanuel-Thomas" title="Jay Emmanuel-Thomas">Jay Emmanuel-Thomas</a> who also joined Cardiff City on loan in January 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Ramsey was handed his first start for Cardiff against <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Ramsey again started for Cardiff City in the <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_derby" title="South Wales derby">South Wales derby</a> against <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a> where he provided an assist for <a href="/wiki/Craig_Bellamy" title="Craig Bellamy">Craig Bellamy</a> in the game ending 1–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Ramsey again completed 90 minutes for Cardiff in the game against <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>. A minor thigh strain ruled Ramsey out of the match against Nottingham Forest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> He made his come back against <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>, scoring in a 2–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 February, Cardiff asked for a loan extension until the end of the season with a 24-hour call back option; however, Arsenal turned this offer down and Ramsey returned to Arsenal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.E2.80.9311">2010–11</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010–11">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">
<p>Scoring the goal was a special moment for me. This was worth the wait and so many people have helped me through the tough time I had, hopefully this will give them the same satisfaction as it does me.</p>
</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">— Ramsey on his first goal of the 2010–11 season<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The midfielder ended the season with seven league appearances.</p>
<p>Ramsey made his Arsenal return as a 72nd-minute substitute against Manchester United in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_FA_Cup" title="2010–11 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> which Arsenal lost 2–0. He made his first start since his injury for Arsenal on 19 March against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>. On 1 May, Ramsey scored his first goal of the season in a 1–0 home <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Premier_League" title="2010–11 Premier League">Premier League</a> victory over Manchester United. He also won the Man of the Match award.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.9312">2011–12</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2011–12">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey_16.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2157" data-file-width="1092" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Aaron_Ramsey_16.jpg/150px-Aaron_Ramsey_16.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Aaron_Ramsey_16.jpg/225px-Aaron_Ramsey_16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Aaron_Ramsey_16.jpg/300px-Aaron_Ramsey_16.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey_16.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ramsey warming up before a match against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> on 24 March 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 16 August 2011, Ramsey made his first <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2011–12 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> appearance of the season at home against <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a>. In the fourth minute of the match he assisted on <a href="/wiki/Theo_Walcott" title="Theo Walcott">Theo Walcott</a>'s goal that gave Arsenal the 1–0 advantage in the first leg of the match. Four days later he played a league game at the Emirates Stadium against Liverpool where on the 78th minute of play, <a href="/wiki/Ignasi_Miquel" title="Ignasi Miquel">Ignasi Miquel</a>'s attempted clearance hit Ramsey and looped into the back of the net past <a href="/wiki/Wojciech_Szcz%C4%99sny" title="Wojciech Szczęsny">Wojciech Szczęsny</a> for an own goal. The game finished 2–0 to Liverpool.</p>
<p>On 17 September 2011, Ramsey assisted on <a href="/wiki/Mikel_Arteta" title="Mikel Arteta">Mikel Arteta</a> for Arsenal's second goal as the team lost 4–3 away to <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Premier_League" title="2011–12 Premier League">Premier League</a> game. He was widely criticised for his performance lately for slowing down the tempo of the game and being indecisive in passing. However, he had a solid game during a convincing 3–0 Premier League win against <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> on 24 September 2011. He provided an assist for the Arsenal captain <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a> by a through ball in less than one minute after the half-time break. He made another important through pass to Theo Walcott on the 54th minute that saw <a href="/wiki/David_Wheater" title="David Wheater">David Wheater</a> sent off for pulling Walcott from the back.</p>
<p>On 19 October 2011, he scored a dramatic last minute winner against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympique_Marseille" title="Olympique Marseille">Olympique Marseille</a> in an important <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2011–12 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a> match of the Champions League. On 23 October 2011, Ramsey assisted <a href="/wiki/Gervinho" title="Gervinho">Gervinho</a> for the first goal in a 3–1 win for the Gunners. He scored the equaliser on 11 February 2012 in a 2–1 win away to <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.9313">2012–13</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2012–13">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ramsey was a substitute for Arsenal's first four league games of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Arsenal_F.C._season" title="2012–13 Arsenal F.C. season">2012–13 season</a>. On 15 September he replaced <a href="/wiki/Francis_Coquelin" title="Francis Coquelin">Francis Coquelin</a> before hitting the post in the buildup to Arsenal's fifth goal in a 6–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a>. On 23 September, he made his first start of the season against defending champions <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_City_FC" title="Manchester City FC">Manchester City</a>, impressing in the right flank role. On 3 October, Ramsey scored a chip shot with his right foot in a 3–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_F.C." title="Olympiacos F.C.">Olympiacos</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a> match.</p>
<p>On 19 December 2012, it was announced that Ramsey, along with teammates <a href="/wiki/Alex_Oxlade-Chamberlain" title="Alex Oxlade-Chamberlain">Alex Oxlade-Chamberlain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kieran_Gibbs" title="Kieran Gibbs">Kieran Gibbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Wilshere" title="Jack Wilshere">Jack Wilshere</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Jenkinson" title="Carl Jenkinson">Carl Jenkinson</a>, had signed a new long-term contract with Arsenal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Due to his rise in form, he was voted man of the match in two consecutive games by the Arsenal fans on Arsenal.com against <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>. Ramsey was voted as Arsenal Player of the Month award by the fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> He followed this up by scoring his first league goal of the season in the 4–1 victory against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C" title="Wigan Athletic F.C">Wigan Athletic</a>, which saw the Lancashire-based club relegated from the Premier League.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013.E2.80.9314">2013–14</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2013–14">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey_v_Cardiff_2013_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2987" data-file-width="1814" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Aaron_Ramsey_v_Cardiff_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/200px-Aaron_Ramsey_v_Cardiff_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Aaron_Ramsey_v_Cardiff_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Aaron_Ramsey_v_Cardiff_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Aaron_Ramsey_v_Cardiff_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/400px-Aaron_Ramsey_v_Cardiff_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey_v_Cardiff_2013_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ramsey facing former club <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> in the Premier League in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ramsey started the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Arsenal_F.C._season" title="2013–14 Arsenal F.C. season">2013–14 season</a> well, scoring in the first leg of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> play-off against <a href="/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e_S.K._(football)" title="Fenerbahçe S.K. (football)">Fenerbahçe</a> and claiming the <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_match" title="Man of the match">Man of the Match</a> award. In the return leg, he scored twice to end the tie 5–0 on aggregate and secure Arsenal's place in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a>. Ramsey continued his fine form in Arsenal's 3–1 win over Fulham in the second round of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">Premier League</a>, helping <a href="/wiki/Olivier_Giroud" title="Olivier Giroud">Olivier Giroud</a> score the first goal via a deflection, and being named Man of the Match. The absence of <a href="/wiki/Mikel_Arteta" title="Mikel Arteta">Mikel Arteta</a> from Arsenal's midfield saw Arsène Wenger field Ramsey in a deeper midfield role as opposed to 2011–12, and Ramsey thrived in the new role, with another inspired midfield performance against <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_London_derby" title="North London derby">North London derby</a> on 2 September, where he was involved in the build-up play to Giroud's goal. He then scored twice against Sunderland on 14 September, with his first goal being a first-touch volley, and the second involving build-up play with Giroud and new signing <a href="/wiki/Mesut_%C3%96zil" title="Mesut Özil">Mesut Özil</a>.</p>
<p>Ramsey continued his excellent form by scoring in Arsenal's 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Marseille</a> in the Champions League at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_V%C3%A9lodrome" title="Stade Vélodrome">Stade Vélodrome</a> and scoring the opener in a 3–1 Premier League win against Stoke City four days later. On 28 September, he was again named as the Man of the Match as he netted another goal and claimed an assist in the away game against <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>, which Arsenal won 2–1. Three days later, in a game against <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> in a Champions League fixture, he set up Özil's first goal for Arsenal. Ramsey won the Barclays Premier League player of the month award for September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ARS-OM_1314_Ramsey_free_kick_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1798" data-file-width="1753" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/ARS-OM_1314_Ramsey_free_kick_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-ARS-OM_1314_Ramsey_free_kick_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/ARS-OM_1314_Ramsey_free_kick_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-ARS-OM_1314_Ramsey_free_kick_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/ARS-OM_1314_Ramsey_free_kick_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-ARS-OM_1314_Ramsey_free_kick_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ARS-OM_1314_Ramsey_free_kick_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ramsey taking a free kick in a Champions League match against <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Marseille</a> on 26 November 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 19 October, he scored a solo goal against <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>, which was his ninth goal for Arsenal in the season, before assisting the fourth Arsenal goal in a 4–1 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> His good form continued into November as he scored a spectacular long range shot from outside of the box in a 2–0 win against Liverpool on 2 November to put Arsenal five points clear at the top of the Premier League table with ten games played.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> He also scored a crucial second-half header four days later against <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> in a 1–0 away victory in the Champions League group stages, bringing his goal tally to 13 in 21 appearances for club and country. On 30 November, he scored two goals against his former club Cardiff City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> On 26 December, he suffered a thigh strain in Arsenal's away fixture against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> eventually missing over three months of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ramsey's early season form saw him voted Arsenal's <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Arsenal_F.C._season#Arsenal_Player_of_the_Month_award" title="2013–14 Arsenal F.C. season">Player of the Month</a> for four consecutive months between August and November 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On 18 March 2014, he signed a new contract extension with the <i>Gunners</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 April, Ramsey returned from injury as a substitute in Arsenal's 3–0 loss at <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On 12 April, he was named in the starting line-up for the first time since <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_FA_Cup" title="2013–14 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-final against <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a>, playing 113 minutes before being substituted for <a href="/wiki/Kim_K%C3%A4llstr%C3%B6m" title="Kim Källström">Kim Källström</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> On 20 April, he scored once and was credited with two assists in Arsenal's 3–0 win away to <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 April, Ramsey was named as one of the six players on the shortlist for the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> award,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> and on 11 May he scored a volley to help his side to a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> on the last day of the Premier League 2013–14 season, relegating their opponents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> On 17 May, Ramsey scored the winning goal in the 109th minute of the <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Cup_Final" title="2014 FA Cup Final">2014 FA Cup Final</a> against Hull City, ending Arsenal's nine-year wait for a trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 June 2014, Ramsey was named Arsenal's Player of the Season after his performance of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Arsenal_F.C._season" title="2013–14 Arsenal F.C. season">2013–14 season</a> with 58 percent of the votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arsenal.com_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-arsenal.com-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.E2.80.9315">2014–15</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2014–15">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giroud_celebrates_his_goal_1_(16235400319).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2386" data-file-width="3580" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Giroud_celebrates_his_goal_1_%2816235400319%29.jpg/220px-Giroud_celebrates_his_goal_1_%2816235400319%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Giroud_celebrates_his_goal_1_%2816235400319%29.jpg/330px-Giroud_celebrates_his_goal_1_%2816235400319%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Giroud_celebrates_his_goal_1_%2816235400319%29.jpg/440px-Giroud_celebrates_his_goal_1_%2816235400319%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giroud_celebrates_his_goal_1_(16235400319).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ramsey (second from right)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ramsey started the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Arsenal_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Arsenal F.C. season">2014–15 season</a> by scoring Arsenal's second goal in their 3–0 victory of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Community_Shield" title="2014 FA Community Shield">Community Shield</a> on 10 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Six days later, in the club's first league match of the season, at home against <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>, he scored the winning goal in injury-time to secure a 2–1 comeback victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> On 19 August, in the first leg of Arsenal's Champions League play-off away to <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%9Fikta%C5%9F_J.K." title="Beşiktaş J.K.">Beşiktaş</a>, he was sent off for a second booking in a goalless draw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Four days later, he scored in 2–2 draw at <a href="/wiki/Goodison_Park" title="Goodison Park">Goodison Park</a> against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Everton_F.C" title="Everton F.C">Everton</a>.</p>
<p>On 3 December, Ramsey assisted <a href="/wiki/Alexis_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Alexis Sánchez">Alexis Sánchez</a>'s late winner against <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> at home. The following league fixture saw him scoring a volley against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C" title="Stoke City F.C">Stoke City</a> in a thrilling 3–2 defeat at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Britannia_Stadium" title="Britannia Stadium">Britannia</a>, ending a three-month goal drought in the process. On 9 December, he scored two goals against <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a> in Arsenal's last group stage match in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>, helping Arsenal to a 4–1 win and second position in the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> On 4 May, Ramsey scored Arsenal's second goal in a 1–3 away league win at <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> On 30 May 2015, Ramsey was selected to start in the <a href="/wiki/2015_FA_Cup_Final" title="2015 FA Cup Final">2015 FA Cup Final</a>, playing the full 90 minutes in a 4–0 win over Aston Villa at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015.E2.80.9316">2015–16</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2015–16">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ramsey scored his first goal of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Arsenal_F.C._season" title="2015–16 Arsenal F.C. season">2015–16 season</a> in a 3–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> on 17 October at <a href="/wiki/Vicarage_Road" title="Vicarage Road">Vicarage Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On 8 March, Ramsey suffered a thigh injury in a 4–0 away victory over <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_FA_Cup" title="2015–16 FA Cup">FA Cup replay</a>, and was ruled out for five weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016.E2.80.9317">2016–17</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2016–17">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Mikel_Arteta" title="Mikel Arteta">Mikel Arteta</a>'s departure, Ramsey was handed the number 8 jersey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ramsey101.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="560" height="314" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ramsey101.jpg/220px-Ramsey101.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ramsey101.jpg/330px-Ramsey101.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ramsey101.jpg/440px-Ramsey101.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ramsey101.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aaron Ramsey (middle) lines up for Wales Under-21 alongside <a href="/wiki/Christian_Ribeiro" title="Christian Ribeiro">Christian Ribeiro</a> (right) and <a href="/wiki/Ched_Evans" title="Ched Evans">Ched Evans</a> (left)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ramsey had his first taste of international action when he was called up for the Wales U17s in 2005. A part of the new wave of young talents to emerge from the Wales youth teams, he debuted for the U21 side on 21 August 2007 in a 4–3 away win over <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_under-21_football_team" title="Sweden national under-21 football team">Sweden U21s</a> several months shy of his seventeenth birthday, breaking former club mate <a href="/wiki/Chris_Gunter" title="Chris Gunter">Chris Gunter</a>'s record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Youth coach <a href="/wiki/Brian_Flynn" title="Brian Flynn">Brian Flynn</a> revealed that Ramsey had been purposely held back in the U21s to help qualify for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_UEFA_European_Under-21_Football_Championship" title="2009 UEFA European Under-21 Football Championship">2009 U21 European Championships</a> but they lost a close contest to England U21s in the play-offs, where Ramsey himself scored a volley with his weaker foot in the second leg at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Villa_Park_(stadium)" title="Villa Park (stadium)">Villa Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ramsey made his debut for the <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales national football team</a> on 19 November 2008, aged 17, playing 88 minutes of a 1–0 away win in <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> On 14 October 2009, he scored his first senior goal in the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2010 World Cup qualifier</a> away at Liechtenstein from a free kick awarded for a trip on <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Bale" title="Gareth Bale">Gareth Bale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> As the World Cup qualification campaign came to an end, he and 11 other senior internationals were recalled to Flynn's preliminary U21 squad on 30 October for a qualifier but later withdrew.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On 6 November, Toshack also called him up for the 14 November friendly against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Wales won 3–0 and Ramsey was involved in all of them – assisting <a href="/wiki/David_Edwards_(footballer)" title="David Edwards (footballer)">David Edwards</a>' opener, setting up <a href="/wiki/Joe_Ledley" title="Joe Ledley">Joe Ledley</a> to assist the second and then scoring a solo effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Ramsey was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Wales" title="Football Association of Wales">FAW</a>'s Young Player of the Year award that same month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manager <a href="/wiki/Gary_Speed" title="Gary Speed">Gary Speed</a> appointed Ramsey as permanent captain of Wales, beginning with the match against England on 26 March 2011. This made him the youngest ever Wales captain at the age of 20 years 90 days, beating the record set by <a href="/wiki/Mike_England" title="Mike England">Mike England</a> in 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> He scored his first goal as captain in Wales' final <a href="/wiki/Nations_Cup_(football)" title="Nations Cup (football)">Nations Cup</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland national football team">Northern Ireland</a> on 27 May 2011.</p>
<p>Ramsey was one of five Welshmen selected to compete at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Olympic Football Tournament</a> for <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Olympic_football_team" title="Great Britain Olympic football team">Great Britain</a>. He featured in all three group games, the latter two as a starter. In the quarter-finals against <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_under-23_football_team" title="South Korea national under-23 football team">South Korea</a> on 4 August at Cardiff's <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a>, he equalised with a penalty kick and the match finished 1–1; he scored again in the <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout" title="Penalty shootout">penalty shootout</a> which his team lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Williams_(footballer)" title="Ashley Williams (footballer)">Ashley Williams</a> was appointed captain of Wales by Chris Coleman, replacing Ramsey after a run of defeats, but the manager said Ramsey would most likely be captain of Wales again in his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> On 22 March 2013, Ramsey scored an equalising 73rd-minute penalty in a 2–1 victory over British rivals <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_A" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group A">Group A World Cup qualification fixture</a>, however he received a red card for a foul on <a href="/wiki/James_McArthur" title="James McArthur">James McArthur</a> during added time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scotland_1_Wales_2_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scotland_1_Wales_2-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_goals">International goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td>1.</td>
<td>4 August 2012</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, Wales</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey_vs_Swansea_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5184" data-file-width="3456" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Aaron_Ramsey_vs_Swansea_2011.jpg/200px-Aaron_Ramsey_vs_Swansea_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Aaron_Ramsey_vs_Swansea_2011.jpg/300px-Aaron_Ramsey_vs_Swansea_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Aaron_Ramsey_vs_Swansea_2011.jpg/400px-Aaron_Ramsey_vs_Swansea_2011.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aaron_Ramsey_vs_Swansea_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ramsey on the ball against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swansea_City_F.C." title="Swansea City F.C.">Swansea</a> in the Premier League in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">2013–14 Premier League</a> season, Aaron Ramsey developed into one of Arsenal's most influential players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Arsenal's manager <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> has described Ramsey as a "complete midfielder," and stated: "I was a midfielder, and I would have loved to have had what he has. He can defend, he can attack, he can score goals. What more do you want?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Ramsey was rewarded for his outstanding form during the 2013–14 season by being named Arsenal's Player of the Season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ramsey blends superior technique with a powerful running style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Long known for his technical ability, during the 2013–14 Premier League season, Ramsey also developed into a strong runner with the ball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Wenger observed, "[Ramsey] is now brushing opponents off and running away from them with ease."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The Arsenal website's first team biography series writes that Ramsey possesses "a mixture of tireless energy, strong technique, tigerish tackling and quick transitions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-date_of_birth_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-date_of_birth-1">[1]</a></sup> Former Arsenal midfielder <a href="/wiki/Ray_Parlour" title="Ray Parlour">Ray Parlour</a> said that Ramsey could "become as influential as <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2013, Ramsey was ranked alongside <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Yaya_Tour%C3%A9" title="Yaya Touré">Yaya Touré</a> as the best central midfielder in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">2013–14 Premier League</a> season. Ramsey had touched the ball more times than any other player (1,115) and had made the most tackles (57).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> On 24 December 2013, Ramsey and Touré were reported to be the only two players in the Premier League to have completed more than 1,000 passes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite missing over three months of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">2013–14 Premier League</a>, Ramsey remained the Arsenal player who has won the most tackles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> He was also the team's second-top scorer for the season (16 goals),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> and provided the second-highest number of assists for the season (8).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2015, former Liverpool player Steven Gerrard hailed Ramsey as "the best attacking midfielder in the Premier League".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ramsey married childhood sweetheart Colleen Rowlands at <a href="/wiki/Caldicot_Castle" title="Caldicot Castle">Caldicot Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Monmouthshire" title="Monmouthshire">Monmouthshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> on 8 June 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Ramsey is a supporter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a> and has spoken of his "passion" for animals and their conservation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In January 2014 Ramsey signed a modelling contract with <a href="/wiki/Elite_Model_Management" title="Elite Model Management">Elite Model Management</a> London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id=".22The_Curse_of_Aaron_Ramsey.22">"The Curse of Aaron Ramsey"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title='Edit section: "The Curse of Aaron Ramsey"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since 2011, Ramsey has been associated with a mythical curse called "the Ramsey effect", meaning that almost every time he scores a goal, someone famous dies within days. His first so-called "victim" was <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>, who was killed on 2 May 2011, the day after Ramsey scored the only goal of the game in Arsenal's 1–0 Premier League win over Manchester United. This was followed by a goal against Tottenham on 2 October; <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> co-founder <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> died three days later. On 19 October, Ramsey came off the bench to score the winner against Marseille in the Champions League and Libyan leader <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a> was killed the following day. On 11 February 2012, Ramsey again came off the bench to score his final goal of the 2011–12 season, this time the equaliser in a 2–1 victory over Sunderland. Later that day, American singer <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a> was found dead. These four deaths prompted the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i> to run a story about how Ramsey was believed to somehow be involved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Talk of a "curse" returned in late August 2013 when Ramsey scored twice in Arsenal's 2–0 victory in the Champions League against Fenerbahçe; interviewer Sir <a href="/wiki/David_Frost" title="David Frost">David Frost</a> and Irish poet <a href="/wiki/Seamus_Heaney" title="Seamus Heaney">Seamus Heaney</a> died three and four days later, respectively. Other celebrities whose deaths have been linked to the Ramsey effect are actor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Walker" title="Paul Walker">Paul Walker</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latin_Times_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Latin_Times-115">[115]</a></sup> actor/comedian <a href="/wiki/Robin_Williams" title="Robin Williams">Robin Williams</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latin_Times_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Latin_Times-115">[115]</a></sup> actor/filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Richard_Attenborough" title="Richard Attenborough">Richard Attenborough</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latin_Times_115-2"><a href="#cite_note-Latin_Times-115">[115]</a></sup> and former First Lady of the United States <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Reagan" title="Nancy Reagan">Nancy Reagan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> died the day after Ramsey scored in Arsenal's 3–1 <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> win over Sunderland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europe_Newsweek_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europe_Newsweek-117">[117]</a></sup> and actor <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rickman" title="Alan Rickman">Alan Rickman</a> died on 14 January 2016; Ramsey had scored in a 3-3 draw with Liverpool the night before. The latest 'victims' are the singer <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a> on 25 December 2016, the former President of Portugal <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_Soares" title="Mário Soares">Mário Soares</a> on 7 January 2017, the Iranian politician and ex-president, <a href="/wiki/Akbar_Hashemi_Rafsanjani" title="Akbar Hashemi Rafsanjani">Akbar Hashemi Rafsanjani</a> a day later and the former manager of the England football team <a href="/wiki/Graham_Taylor" title="Graham Taylor">Graham Taylor</a> on 12 January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europe_Newsweek_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europe_Newsweek-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>The "curse", according to many Internet users, allegedly led to the historic victory of the "Leave" option during the 2016 UK referendum on EU membership one day after Wales won 3-0 against Russia during Euro 2016, Ramsey's scores contributing to the football victory of the Welsh national team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ramsey never publicly spoke about the Ramsey effect until August 2015. In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Sport_(UK_magazine)" title="Sport (UK magazine)"><i>Sport</i> magazine</a>, he said, "The most ridiculous rumour I've heard is that people die after I score. There have been loads of occasions where I've scored and somebody has died. That's just a crazy rumour. Although I took out some baddies!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual">Individual</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aaron_Ramsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Individual">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>London Player of the Year: 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_statistics#Assists" title="UEFA Euro 2016 statistics">UEFA European Championship</a> top assists: <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016#statistics" title="UEFA Euro 2016">2016</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
